                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-94862650592">
                      #Daydream: Glacier National Park
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-94862650592" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="author-name Font-C-2-140 D-b">
                            <a class="attribution-name Font-C-2-140 Fw-b Whs-n" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:ffc3363f-194a-317f-a08b-4dcc92eb11e6;t9:17;elm:itm;elmt:link;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/marrry/14673699479/" style="color:#000;" target="_blank">
                             Photo by Mary Haynes
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             August 18, 2014
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-94862650592" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           We know how it is. Youre stuck at your desk and the day seems to be going on forever. Your mind starts to wander  at first to anywhere but here, but then to exotic, faraway lands where your everyday problems and stress melt in the presence of true paradise. You want to go to there, and we want to go with you. Every day at 3 p.m. Eastern, well send you a picture of the place we at Yahoo Travel are daydreaming about so we can all take that mental vacation together. Lets go to
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="#Daydream: Glacier National Park" height="375" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/a585b47779c806221d8ad5a1bd11c23c791b7a94.jpg" width="500"/>
                          <em>
                           (Photo:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ffc3363f-194a-317f-a08b-4dcc92eb11e6;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/marrry/14673699479/" target="_blank">
                            Mary Haynes/Flickr
                           </a>
                           )
                          </em>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           Glacier National Park in Montana. The 700 miles of hiking trails are just what were daydreaming about now that weve just bought a new pair of killer hiking boots online. This would be the perfect place to break them in
                          </em>
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                        </div>
                       </div>

root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

Skyscanner survey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;found that&#xA0;only one percent of people actually prefer the middle seat on a plane. No surprise there. But Frontier Airlines may change all that.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe budget airline plans to stop the middle seat haters with its new 19-inch middle seats, according to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cntraveler.com\u002Fstories\u002F2015-07-09\u002Fthe-one-airline-that-s-actually-improving-the-middle-seat\"\u003Ecntraveler.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. That size is one inch wider than Frontier&#x2019;s window and aisle seats and, the airline claims, wider than on any other U.S. airline.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnother bonus? Frontier does not plan to charge more for the wider middle seats.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESound too good to be true? It&#x2019;s not: There are downsides. The seats will have less padding; passengers in these seats will be closer to the seat in front of them and behind them (less pitch), which affects legroom; and the seats do not recline (though Frontier calls them&#xA0;&#x201C;pre-reclined&#x201D;).&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo avoid all these pitfalls, a traveler would still have to purchase&#xA0;a middle seat in the more expensive premium economy &#x201C;Stretch&#x201D; section.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fthe-new-airline-seat-that-turns-economy-into-business-101370413642.html\"\u003EThe New Airline Seat That Turns Economy Into Business Class\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps the inch of extra room in the middle seat is to offset some of the other changes coming to Frontier. According to cntraveler.com, this year the airline is adding 12 seats to every Airbus A320 and A319 it flies. Greenlands Finest Microbrew Beers","summary":"I'm a beer woman. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EAnybody who knows me knows I don&#x2019;t drink vodka. I don&#x2019;t do tequila. And I&#x2019;ve never been a big fan of anything that comes with a garnish. I am, however, a beer girl. Raised in Cincinnati, a town with German roots, I have a deep love of hops, and over the years my tastes have been refined from \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhudepohlbeer.com\u002F\"\u003EHudepohl\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and Schlitz to craft beers. Don&#x2019;t get me wrong &#x2014; when stuck on a riverboat for a bachelorette party in, say, Austin, Texas (thanks to my sister Emily), I will still happily down a Bud, a Coors, or a Schlitz. But I have learned to appreciate the fine craft of beer making and love a small-batch brew. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Ffinger-pulling-head-pulling-and-kick-the-seal-122521580652.html\"\u003EFinger Pulling and Kick the Seal &#x2014; Welcome to the Arctic Games!\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F93fb6d09ed4cf36c50b1cd8100b9a9da95be5f9d.png\" alt=\"Taste-Testing Greenland&#x2019;s Finest Microbrew Beers\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Godthaab Bryghus brewery is in a building that conveniently also houses a dive bar called Daddy&#x2019;s. While &#x201C;Daddy&#x201D; is a great guy named Gert, the actual brewery is run by Mikael Sorenson, who swears that the beer there is made with glacier ice that is at least 2,000 years old.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Yes, we have men who go out onto the ice and cut slabs off the glaciers for us and bring them back here for our beer,&#x201D; Sorenson said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E[Side note: Apparently ice cutting is a big business. Down the street is an ice cream shop that also uses 2,000-year-old ice. &#x201C;Ice cream in Greenland?&#x201D; you may be asking. &#x201C;Isn&#x2019;t it cold enough?&#x201D; No. It&#x2019;s not. Greenland has the second largest ice cream consumption per capita in the world, second only to Finland. Go figure.]\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3a590de53797cb2f646953e3212a190735cb2dff.png\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhile there are no official stats on how much beer is consumed in &#xA0;Nuuk, Greenland&#x2019;s capital, judging by the crowds in the bars and the continual snow, I&#x2019;d say it ranks right up there. And frankly, I can&#x2019;t say I blame them &#x2014; the weather is rough (see previous episode: &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x201D;), and the beer is delicious. At the time I visited, there were five beers on tap, including the Musk Ox, the Eric the Red, and the Polar Bear (they like to name the beers after local animals). And here&#x2019;s a tip: While they are all delicious, if you ever find yourself at Daddy&#x2019;s in Nuuk, ask for Gert and Mikael and get them to give you the unfiltered versions of all the beers. They may smell like dirty feet, but they taste like heaven.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere is only one problem with the Godthaab Bryghus beer &#x2014; while it is possibly the best beer I have ever tasted (and trust: I have tasted a lot of beer), they don&#x2019;t export. So to get 2,000-year-old glacier-water beer, you have to go to the source. It&#x2019;s worth it. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELet Yahoo Travel inspire you every day.
